Other aspects of Humboldt's life and career
-------------------------------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Other aspects of Humboldt's life and career")]

### Humboldt and the Prussian monarchy

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Humboldt and the Prussian monarchy")]

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg/250px-AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg)

Humboldt's [seal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seal_(emblem) "Seal (emblem)") on a private letter

In the Napoleonic wars, Prussia had capitulated to France, signing the [Treaty of Tilsit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Tilsit "Treaty of Tilsit"). The Prussian royal family returned to Berlin, but sought better terms of the treaty and [Friedrich Wilhelm III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm_III "Friedrich Wilhelm III") commissioned his younger brother [Prince Wilhelm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Wilhelm_of_Prussia_(1783%E2%80%931851) "Prince Wilhelm of Prussia (1783–1851)") with this. Friedrich Wilhelm III asked Alexander to be part of the mission, charged with introducing the prince to Paris society. This turn of events for Humboldt could not have been better, since he desired to live in Paris rather than Berlin.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Terra1955210-200)

In 1814 Humboldt accompanied the allied sovereigns to London. Three years later he was summoned by the king of Prussia to attend him at the [congress of Aachen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1818) "Congress of Aix-la-Chapelle (1818)"). Again in the autumn of 1822 he accompanied the same monarch to the [Congress of Verona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Verona "Congress of Verona"), proceeded thence with the royal party to Rome and Naples and returned to Paris in the spring of 1823. Humboldt had long regarded Paris as his true home. Thus, when at last he received from his sovereign a summons to join his court at Berlin, he obeyed reluctantly.

Between 1830 and 1848 Humboldt was frequently employed in diplomatic missions to the court of [King Louis Philippe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis-Philippe_of_France "Louis-Philippe of France") of France, with whom he always maintained the most cordial personal relations. [Charles X of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_X_of_France "Charles X of France") had been overthrown, with Louis-Philippe of the [house of Orléans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Orl%C3%A9ans "House of Orléans") becoming king. Humboldt knew the family, and he was sent by the Prussian monarch to Paris to report on events to his monarch. He spent three years in France, from 1830 to 1833. His friends [François Arago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Arago "François Arago") and [François Guizot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Guizot "François Guizot"), were appointed to posts in Louis-Philippe's government.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Terra1955311-201)

Humboldt's brother, [Wilhelm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt "Wilhelm von Humboldt"), died on 8 April 1835. Alexander lamented that he had lost half of himself with the death of his brother. Upon the accession of the crown prince [Frederick William IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_William_IV_of_Prussia "Frederick William IV of Prussia") in June 1840, Humboldt's favor at court increased. Indeed, the new king's craving for Humboldt's company became at times so importunate as to leave him only a few waking hours to work on his writing.

### Representation of indigenous population

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Representation of indigenous population")]

Humboldt's publications such as _Personal Narrative of Travels to the Equinoctial Regions of the New Continent during the years 1799–1804_ originate from a time when colonialism was prevalent. Within recent academic publications, there are arguments for and against Humboldt's own imperial bias. Within the book _Imperial Eyes_, [Pratt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Louise_Pratt "Mary Louise Pratt") argues for an implicit imperial bias within Humboldt's writing.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Pratt-2008-202) While Humboldt financed his expedition to the Spanish colonies independently, the Spanish monarchy allowed him to travel to South America.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Pratt-2008-202) Due to unrest within the Spanish colonies in South America, the Spanish crown implemented liberal reforms which led to greater support of the Spanish monarchy within the lower class.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Pratt-2008-202) However, Pratt points out that the reforms created opposition towards the Spanish rule within the upper class as the declining control of the Spanish monarchy would result in the white South American elite losing their privileges.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Pratt-2008-202) When Humboldt wrote about the natural world within South America, he portrayed it as neutral and free of people: If the indigenous population was mentioned within Humboldt's writing, Pratt argues, they were only represented when they were beneficial for Europeans.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Pratt-2008-202) Others argue that Humboldt was a German Columbus, as he described a virginal country that could be used for commerce by Europeans.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Wilke-2011-203)

Other scholars counter Pratt's argumentation and refer to the abolitionist and anti-colonialist standpoint that Humboldt represents within his writing. An example is Humboldt's descriptions of the South American colonies in which he critiqued Spanish colonial rule.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-204) His close relationship with Enlightenment values such as liberty and freedom led to his support of democracy and his subsequent support of the independence of South America.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Wulf_2015-205) In order to improve the material and political situation of the indigenous population, Humboldt included propositions within his writing that he also presented to the Spanish monarchy.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Wilke-2011-203) When witnessing a slave market, Humboldt was shocked by the treatment of black people which led him to become opposed to slavery and support the abolitionist movement throughout his life.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Wulf_2015-205) Within his descriptions in _Personal Narratives_, Humboldt also included the answers that were given to him by indigenous people. Additionally, Lubrich[_[who?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual\_of\_Style/Words\_to\_watch#Unsupported\_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")_] argues that despite the colonial and orientalist notions of his writing, Humboldt did not recreate these stereotypes, but deconstructed them.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Wilke-2011-203)

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg/250px-Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg)

Portrait of Humboldt by [Julius Schrader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Schrader "Julius Schrader"), 1859. [Metropolitan Museum of Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art "Metropolitan Museum of Art")

Because Humboldt did not mention God in his work _Cosmos_, and sometimes spoke unfavourably of religious attitudes, it was occasionally speculated that he was a [materialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Materialism "Materialism") philosopher, or perhaps an [atheist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheist "Atheist").[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-206) However, unlike irreligious figures such as [Robert G. Ingersoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_G._Ingersoll "Robert G. Ingersoll"), who went so far as to use Humboldtian science to campaign against religion,[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-207) Humboldt himself denied imputations of atheism. In a letter to [Varnhagen von Ense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_August_Varnhagen_von_Ense "Karl August Varnhagen von Ense") he emphasized that he believed the world had indeed been created, writing of _Cosmos_: "...'creation' and the 'created world' are never lost sight of in the book. And did I not, only eight months ago, in the French translation, say, in the plainest terms: 'It is this necessity of things, this occult but permanent connection, this periodical return in the progress, development of formation, phenomena, and events which constitute 'Nature' submissive to a controlling power?'"[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-208)

It has been argued that "although Humboldt emphasizes the basis of morality in the nature of man, he does acknowledge that a belief in God is linked directly to acts of virtue" and therefore "the dignity of man lies at the centre of Humboldt's religious thought".[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-209)

Humboldt also believed firmly in an [afterlife](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afterlife "Afterlife").[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJames191358-210) A letter he wrote to his friend Charlotte Hildebrand Diede states: "God constantly appoints the course of nature and of circumstances; so that, including his existence in an eternal future, the happiness of the individual does not perish, but on the contrary grows and increases."[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-211)

Humboldt remained distant of organized religion, typical of a Protestant in Germany relating to the Catholic Church; Humboldt held deep respect for the ideal side of religious belief and church life within human communities.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJames191356%E2%80%9358-212) He differentiated between "negative" religions, and those "all positive religions [which] consist of three distinct parts—a code of morals which is nearly the same in all of them, and generally very pure; a geological chimera, and a myth or a little historical novel".[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-213) In _Cosmos_, he wrote about how rich geological descriptions were found in different religious traditions, and stated: "Christianity gradually diffused itself, and, wherever it was adopted as the religion of the state, it not only exercised a beneficial condition on the lower classes by inculcating the social freedom of mankind, but also expanded the views of men in their communion with Nature...this tendency to glorify the Deity in his works gave rise to a taste for natural observation."[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-214)

Humboldt showed [religious tolerance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_tolerance "Religious tolerance") towards Judaism, and he criticized the political _Jews Bill_, which was an initiative intended to establish legal discrimination against Jews. He called this an "abominable" law, since he hoped to see Jews being treated equally in society.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-215)

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg/250px-Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin,_Oranienburger_Str._67_(Gem%C3%A4lde).jpg)

Humboldt in his library in his apartment, [Oranienburger Straße](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oranienburger_Stra%C3%9Fe "Oranienburger Straße"), Berlin, by [Eduard Hildebrandt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eduard_Hildebrandt "Eduard Hildebrandt")

Much of Humboldt's private life remains a mystery because he destroyed his private letters. While a gregarious personality, he may have harbored a sense of social alienation, which drove his passion for escape through travel.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESachs200764-216)

Humboldt never married: while he was friendly with a number of women, including [Henriette](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henriette_Herz "Henriette Herz"), the wife of his mentor Marcus Herz, his sister-in-law Caroline von Humboldt stated "nothing will ever have a great influence on Alexander that doesn't come through men".[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201571-217) He had many strong male friendships, and at times had romances with men.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESachs200765-218)

As a student he became infatuated with Wilhelm Gabriel Wegener, a theology student, penning a succession of letters expressing his "fervent love".[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelferich20048-219) At 25 he met Reinhardt von Haeften (1772–1803), a 22-year-old lieutenant, with whom he lived and travelled for two years, and to whom he wrote in 1794: "I only live through you, my good precious Reinhardt". When von Haeften became engaged, Humboldt begged to remain living with him and his wife: "Even if you must refuse me, treat me coldly with disdain, I should still want to be with you... the love I have for you is not just friendship or brotherly love, it is veneration".[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTERupke2008187%E2%80%93200-220)

A traveling companion in the Americas for five years was [Aimé Bonpland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aim%C3%A9_Bonpland "Aimé Bonpland"), and in [Quito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quito "Quito") in 1802 he met the Ecuadorian aristocrat Don [Carlos Montúfar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Mont%C3%BAfar "Carlos Montúfar"), who travelled with Humboldt to Europe and lived with him. In France, Humboldt travelled and lived with the physicist and balloonist [Joseph Louis Gay-Lussac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Louis_Gay-Lussac "Joseph Louis Gay-Lussac"). Later he had a deep friendship with the married French astronomer [François Arago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Arago "François Arago"), whom he met daily for 15 years.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-221)

Humboldt once wrote "I don't know sensual needs".[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201571-217) However, a pious travelling companion, [Francisco José de Caldas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Jos%C3%A9_de_Caldas "Francisco José de Caldas"), accused him of frequenting houses in Quito where "impure love reigned", of making friends with "obscene dissolute youths", of giving vent to "shameful passions of his heart", and dropping him to travel with "Bonpland and his Adonis" [Montúfar].[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-222)

Humboldt inherited a significant fortune, but the expense of his travels, and most especially of publishing (thirty volumes in all), had by 1834 made him totally reliant on the pension of King Frederick William III.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalls2009109-223) Although he preferred living in Paris, by 1836 the King had insisted he return to Germany. He lived with the Court at [Sanssouci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanssouci "Sanssouci"), and latterly in Berlin, with his valet Seifert, who had accompanied him to Russia in 1829.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Terra1955363-224)

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg/250px-SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg)

Signature of Humboldt late in life, when his handwriting became increasingly difficult to read

Four years before his death, Humboldt executed a deed of gift transferring his entire estate to Seifert,[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalls2009367-225)[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelferich2004312-226) who had by then married and set up a household near Humboldt's apartment. Humboldt had become godfather to his daughter.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Terra1955317-227) The scale of the bequest has always drawn speculation, especially as Seifert was some thirty years younger, and introducing lower class partners into households under the guise of servants was then a common practice.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-228)

In 1908, the sexual researcher [Paul Näcke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_N%C3%A4cke "Paul Näcke") gathered reminiscences from homosexuals[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-229) including Humboldt's friend the botanist [Carl Bolle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Bolle_(naturalist) "Carl Bolle (naturalist)"), then nearly 90 years old: some of the material was incorporated by [Magnus Hirschfeld](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnus_Hirschfeld "Magnus Hirschfeld") into his 1914 study _Homosexuality in Men and Women_.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-230) However, speculations about Humboldt's private life and possible [homosexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexuality "Homosexuality") continue to remain a fractious issue amongst scholars, particularly as earlier biographers had portrayed him as "a largely asexual, Christ-like Humboldt figure...suitable as a national idol".[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTERupke2008195%E2%80%93197-231)

On 24 February 1857, Humboldt suffered a minor [stroke](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stroke "Stroke"), which passed without perceptible symptoms.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClerke1911-232) It was not until the winter of 1858–1859 that his strength began to decline; on 6 May 1859, he died peacefully in Berlin, aged 89. His last words were reported to be "How glorious these sunbeams are! They seem to call Earth to the Heavens!"[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-233) His remains were conveyed in state through the streets of Berlin, in a hearse drawn by six horses. Royal chamberlains led the cortège, each charged with carrying a pillow with Humboldt's medals and other decorations of honor. Humboldt's extended family, descendants of his brother Wilhelm, walked in the procession. Humboldt's coffin was received by the prince-regent at the door of the cathedral. He was interred at the family resting-place at [Tegel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tegel "Tegel"), alongside his brother Wilhelm and sister-in-law Caroline.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Terra1955368%E2%80%93369-234)

Honours and namesakes
---------------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Honours and namesakes")]

The honours which had been showered on Humboldt during their life continued after his death. More species are named after Humboldt than after any other human being.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-Paul-2017-15) The first centenary of Humboldt's birth was celebrated on 14 September 1869, with great enthusiasm in both the New and Old Worlds. Numerous monuments were constructed in his honour, such as [Humboldt Park in Chicago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Park_(Chicago_park) "Humboldt Park (Chicago park)"), planned that year and constructed shortly after the [Chicago fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Chicago_Fire "Great Chicago Fire"). Newly explored regions and species named after Humboldt, as discussed below, also stand as a measure of his wide fame and popularity.

"Scarcely was there a European order which Humboldt had not the right to wear", and "more than a hundred and fifty societies to which he had been elected". These included "the most celebrated Academies of the leading nations of Europe and America, and not merely those of a purely scientific character, but any which had for their object the spread of education and the advancement of civilisation." Additionally, he was at least an honorary member of academies and learned societies throughout Europe and America and "was invested with the degree of Doctor in three faculties".[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873[httpsbabelhathitrustorgcgiptiduc2ark13960t5m903z33view1upseq398skin2021_382]_[[File:PD-icon.svg|12px|class=noviewer|link=|alt=Public_Domain]]&nbsp;This_article_incorporates_[httpswwwlocgovlegal_public_domain_material]_from_websites_or_documents_of_the_[[Library_of_Congress]].[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_incorporating_content_from_public_domain_material_of_the_Library_of_Congress]]-235)

*   1827 [Honorary Doctor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honorary_Doctor "Honorary Doctor") of the [Imperial University of Dorpat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_University_of_Dorpat "Imperial University of Dorpat")[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-236)
*   1829: Actual Privy Counsellor, with the title of Excellency by King [Frederick William III of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_William_III_of_Prussia "Frederick William III of Prussia")[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873106-237)
*   1842: Chancellor of the Order of Merit, an administrative position empowered to appoint, by King [Frederick William IV of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_William_IV_of_Prussia "Frederick William IV of Prussia")[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873282-238)
*   1842: [Pour le Mérite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pour_le_M%C3%A9rite "Pour le Mérite"), Recipient (civil division)[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-239)
*   1844: [Order of the Red Eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_the_Red_Eagle "Order of the Red Eagle"), by King [Frederick William IV of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_William_IV_of_Prussia "Frederick William IV of Prussia")[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873266-240)
*   1847: [Order of the Black Eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_the_Black_Eagle "Order of the Black Eagle"), by King [Frederick William IV of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_William_IV_of_Prussia "Frederick William IV of Prussia"), the highest honour that was in the royal power to confer.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873266-240)
*   1850: Knight Grand Cross of the [Order of Saints Maurice and Lazarus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Saints_Maurice_and_Lazarus "Order of Saints Maurice and Lazarus")[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-241)
*   1852: [Copley Medal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copley_Medal "Copley Medal") "For his eminent services in terrestrial physics"[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873199-242)
*   1853: [Bavarian Maximilian Order for Science and Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bavarian_Maximilian_Order_for_Science_and_Art "Bavarian Maximilian Order for Science and Art") by King [Maximilian II of Bavaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximilian_II_of_Bavaria "Maximilian II of Bavaria") "as the man who honours the order", "the hero of science in Germany".[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruhns1873294-243)
*   1863: Knight Grand Cross of the [Order of Guadalupe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Guadalupe "Order of Guadalupe")[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

### Species named after Humboldt

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Species named after Humboldt")]

Humboldt described many geographical features and species that were hitherto unknown to Europeans. Species named after him include:

*   _Spheniscus humboldti_ – [Humboldt penguin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_penguin "Humboldt penguin")
*   _Dosidicus gigas_ – [Humboldt squid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_squid "Humboldt squid")
*   _[Lilium humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lilium\_humboldtii "Lilium humboldtii")_ – Humboldt's lily
*   _[Phragmipedium humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Phragmipedium\_humboldtii&action=edit&redlink=1 "Phragmipedium humboldtii (page does not exist)")_ – an orchid
*   _[Quercus humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quercus\_humboldtii "Quercus humboldtii")_ – South American (Andean) oak
*   _Conepatus humboldtii_ – [Humboldt's hog-nosed skunk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt%27s_hog-nosed_skunk "Humboldt's hog-nosed skunk")[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-244)
*   _[Annona humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annona\_reticulata "Annona reticulata")_ – Neotropical fruit tree or shrub
*   _[Utricularia humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utricularia\_humboldtii "Utricularia humboldtii")_ – a bladderwort
*   _[Geranium humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geranium\_humboldtii&action=edit&redlink=1 "Geranium humboldtii (page does not exist)")_ – a cranesbill
*   _[Salix humboldtiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salix\_humboldtiana "Salix humboldtiana")_ – a South-American willow[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-245)
*   _[Inia geoffrensis humboldtiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boto "Boto")_ – [Amazon river dolphin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_river_dolphin "Amazon river dolphin") subspecies of [Orinoco River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orinoco_River "Orinoco River") basin
*   _[Rhinocoryne humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rhinocoryne\_humboldti&action=edit&redlink=1 "Rhinocoryne humboldti (page does not exist)")_ – marine snail
*   _[Bathybembix humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bathybembix\_humboldti "Bathybembix humboldti")_ – marine snail
*   _[Rhinella humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhinella\_humboldti "Rhinella humboldti")_ – Rivero's toad
*   _[Pteroglossus humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pteroglossus\_humboldti "Pteroglossus humboldti")_ – Humboldt's Araçari
*   _[Hylocharis humboldtii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hylocharis\_humboldtii "Hylocharis humboldtii")_ – Humboldt's hummingbird
*   _[Casignethus humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Casignethus\_humboldti&action=edit&redlink=1 "Casignethus humboldti (page does not exist)")_ – beetle
*   _[Elzunia humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elzunia\_humboldt "Elzunia humboldt")_ – butterfly
*   †_[Lenisambulatrix humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenisambulatrix\_humboldti "Lenisambulatrix humboldti")_ – Cambrian [Lobopodia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lobopodia "Lobopodia")
*   _[Squamulea humboldtiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Squamulea\_humboldtiana&action=edit&redlink=1 "Squamulea humboldtiana (page does not exist)")_ – lichen[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-246)
*   _[E. (S.) humboldti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eleutherodactylus\_humboldti "Eleutherodactylus humboldti")_[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-247)

*   [![Image 46: Humboldt penguin, native to Chile and Peru](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Spheniscus_humboldti_20070116.jpg/120px-Spheniscus_humboldti_20070116.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Spheniscus_humboldti_20070116.jpg "Humboldt penguin, native to Chile and Peru")

[Humboldt penguin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_penguin "Humboldt penguin"), native to Chile and Peru 
*   [![Image 47: Humboldt squid found in the Humboldt Current](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Dosidicus_gigas.jpg/120px-Dosidicus_gigas.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dosidicus_gigas.jpg "Humboldt squid found in the Humboldt Current")

*   [![Image 48: Quercus humboldtii, an Andean oak](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Quercus_humboldtii_1.JPG/120px-Quercus_humboldtii_1.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Quercus_humboldtii_1.JPG "Quercus humboldtii, an Andean oak")

### Geographical features named after Humboldt

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Geographical features named after Humboldt")]

Features named after him include:[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-248)

*   [Humboldt Bay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Bay_(United_States) "Humboldt Bay (United States)") – Bay in Northern California, United States
*   [Humboldt Current](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Current "Humboldt Current") – off the west coast of South America
*   [Humboldt Glacier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Glacier "Humboldt Glacier") – in North West Greenland
*   [Humboldt River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_River "Humboldt River") and [Humboldt Lake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Lake "Humboldt Lake") – Nevada, United States[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-249)
*   [Humboldt Peak (Colorado)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Peak_(Colorado) "Humboldt Peak (Colorado)")– 4,287 m mountain in Custer County, Colorado, United States
*   [Pico Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pico_Humboldt "Pico Humboldt")– 4,940 m mountain in Mérida, Venezuela
*   [Humboldt Sink](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Sink "Humboldt Sink") – Dry lake bed in Nevada, United States
*   [East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Humboldt_Range "East Humboldt Range") and [West Humboldt Range](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Humboldt_Range "West Humboldt Range") in Nevada, United States
*   [Sima Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sima_Humboldt "Sima Humboldt") – sinkhole in Venezuela
*   "Monumento Nacional Alejandro de Humboldt" at [Caripe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caripe "Caripe"), Venezuela
*   [Mount Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Humboldt "Mount Humboldt")– 1,617 m (5,308 ft), New Caledonia
*   [Humboldt Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Mountains_(Antarctica) "Humboldt Mountains (Antarctica)"), Antarctic mountains discovered and mapped by the [Third German Antarctic Expedition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_German_Antarctic_Expedition "Third German Antarctic Expedition") (1938–1939)
*   [Humboldt Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Mountains_(New_Zealand) "Humboldt Mountains (New Zealand)") – Mountain Range in Fiordland National Park, New Zealand
*   [Humboldt Channel](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Humboldt_Channel_(Canada)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Humboldt Channel (Canada) (page does not exist)") – natural waterway through the central Canadian Arctic Archipelago
*   [Humboldt Falls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Falls "Humboldt Falls")– 275 m Waterfall in Lower Hollyford Valley, Fiordland National Park, New Zealand
*   [Humboldt Redwoods State Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Redwoods_State_Park "Humboldt Redwoods State Park") – in northern California, United States

*   [![Image 49: Humboldt Current](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Humboldt_current.jpg/120px-Humboldt_current.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Humboldt_current.jpg "Humboldt Current")

*   [![Image 50: Pico Humboldt, Venezuela](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Pico_Humboldt.jpg/120px-Pico_Humboldt.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pico_Humboldt.jpg "Pico Humboldt, Venezuela")

### Astronomical features

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Astronomical features")]

*   [54 Alexandra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/54_Alexandra "54 Alexandra") ([asteroid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asteroid "Asteroid"))
*   4877 Humboldt (asteroid)

The mineral [humboldtine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldtine "Humboldtine") was named for Alexander by [Mariano de Rivero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariano_Eduardo_de_Rivero_y_Ustariz "Mariano Eduardo de Rivero y Ustariz") in 1821.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-250)[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-251)

### Universities, colleges, and schools

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Universities, colleges, and schools")]

[![Image 51](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Huberlin-logo.svg/250px-Huberlin-logo.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Huberlin-logo.svg)

Humboldt University of Berlin

*   [Humboldt University of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin "Humboldt University of Berlin") is named after Alexander and his brother [Wilhelm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt "Wilhelm von Humboldt") who founded it[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-252)
*   [Alexander von Humboldt Biological Resources Research Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Biological_Resources_Research_Institute "Alexander von Humboldt Biological Resources Research Institute") in [Bogotá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1 "Bogotá") and [Villa de Leiva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Villa_de_Leiva "Villa de Leiva"), Colombia
*   [California State Polytechnic University, Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_State_Polytechnic_University,_Humboldt "California State Polytechnic University, Humboldt") in [Arcata, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arcata,_California "Arcata, California")
*   [Universidad Alejandro de Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universidad_Alejandro_de_Humboldt "Universidad Alejandro de Humboldt") in Caracas, Venezuela

*   [Alexander-von-Humboldt-Gymnasium, Konstanz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander-von-Humboldt-Gymnasium,_Konstanz "Alexander-von-Humboldt-Gymnasium, Konstanz"), Germany
*   [Alexander von Humboldt German International School Montreal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_German_International_School_Montreal "Alexander von Humboldt German International School Montreal"), Montreal, Canada
*   [Colegio Alemán Alexander von Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colegio_Alem%C3%A1n_Alexander_von_Humboldt_(Mexico_City) "Colegio Alemán Alexander von Humboldt (Mexico City)"), Mexico City, Mexico
*   [Deutsche Schule Lima Alexander von Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Schule_Lima_Alexander_von_Humboldt "Deutsche Schule Lima Alexander von Humboldt"), Lima, Peru
*   [Colegio Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colegio_Humboldt,_Caracas "Colegio Humboldt, Caracas"), Caracas, Venezuela
*   [Humboldt Senior High School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humboldt_Senior_High_School "Humboldt Senior High School"), St. Paul, Minnesota

Alexander von Humboldt also lends his name to a prominent lecture series in [Human geography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_geography "Human geography") in the Netherlands (hosted by the [Radboud University Nijmegen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radboud_University_Nijmegen "Radboud University Nijmegen")). It is the Dutch equivalent of the widely known annual [Hettner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Hettner "Alfred Hettner") lectures at the [University of Heidelberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Heidelberg "University of Heidelberg").

### The Alexander von Humboldt Foundation

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: The Alexander von Humboldt Foundation")]

After his death, Humboldt's friends and colleagues created the [Alexander von Humboldt Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Foundation "Alexander von Humboldt Foundation") (_Stiftung_ in German) to continue his generous support of young academics. Although the original endowment was lost in the [German hyperinflation of the 1920s](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_hyperinflation_of_the_1920s "German hyperinflation of the 1920s"), and again as a result of World War II, the Foundation has been re-endowed by the German government to award young academics and distinguished senior academics from abroad. It plays an important role in attracting foreign researchers to work in Germany and enabling German researchers to work abroad for a period.

[Edgar Allan Poe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe "Edgar Allan Poe") dedicated his last major work, _[Eureka: A Prose Poem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eureka:\_A\_Prose\_Poem "Eureka: A Prose Poem")_, to Humboldt, "With Very Profound Respect". Humboldt's attempt to unify the sciences in his _Kosmos_ was a major inspiration for Poe's project.

In 2019, [Josefina Benedetti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josefina_Benedetti "Josefina Benedetti") composed _Humboldt_ an Orchestral Suite in five movements.

_[Alexander von Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander\_von\_Humboldt\_(ship) "Alexander von Humboldt (ship)")_ is also a German ship named after the scientist, originally built in 1906 by the German shipyard AG Weser at [Bremen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bremen_(city) "Bremen (city)") as _**Reserve Sonderburg**_. She was operated throughout the North and Baltic Seas until being retired in 1986. Subsequently, she was converted into a three-masted [barque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barque "Barque") by the German shipyard Motorwerke Bremerhaven, and was re-launched in 1988 as _Alexander von Humboldt_.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

The [Jan De Nul Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_De_Nul_Group "Jan De Nul Group") operates a hopper dredger built in 1998 also named _Alexander von Humboldt_.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-253)

### Recognitions by contemporaries

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Recognitions by contemporaries")]

[Simón Bolívar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar "Simón Bolívar") wrote that "The real discoverer of South America was Humboldt, since his work was more useful for our people than the work of all conquerors".[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-254)[Charles Darwin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Darwin "Charles Darwin") expressed his debt to Humboldt, and admiration for his work,[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-255) writing to [Joseph Dalton Hooker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Dalton_Hooker "Joseph Dalton Hooker") that Humboldt was the "_greatest scientific traveller who ever lived_".[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-256)[Wilhelm von Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt "Wilhelm von Humboldt") wrote that "Alexander is destined to combine ideas and follow chains of thoughts which would otherwise have remained unknown for ages. His depth, his sharp mind and his incredible speed are a rare combination." [Johann Wolfgang Goethe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_Goethe "Johann Wolfgang Goethe") observed that "Humboldt showers us with true treasures". [Friedrich Schiller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Schiller "Friedrich Schiller") wrote that "Alexander impresses many, particularly when compared to his brother—because he shows off more!" [José de la Luz y Caballero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_la_Luz_y_Caballero "José de la Luz y Caballero") wrote that "Columbus gave Europe a New World; Humboldt made it known in its physical, material, intellectual, and moral aspects".

[Napoléon Bonaparte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte "Napoléon Bonaparte") remarked "You have been studying Botanics? Just like my wife!" [Claude Louis Berthollet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Louis_Berthollet "Claude Louis Berthollet") said "This man is as knowledgeable as a whole academy". [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson") remarked "I consider him the most important scientist whom I have met". [Emil du Bois-Reymond](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emil_du_Bois-Reymond "Emil du Bois-Reymond") wrote that "Every assiduous scholar ... is Humboldt's son; we are all his family."[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-257)[Robert G. Ingersoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_G._Ingersoll "Robert G. Ingersoll") wrote that "He was to science what Shakespeare was to the drama".[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-258)

[Hermann von Helmholtz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_von_Helmholtz "Hermann von Helmholtz") wrote that "During the first half of the present century we had an Alexander von Humboldt, who was able to scan the scientific knowledge of his time in its details, and to bring it within one vast generalization. At the present juncture, it is obviously very doubtful whether this task could be accomplished in a similar way, even by a mind with gifts so peculiarly suited for the purpose as Humboldt's was, and if all his time and work were devoted to the purpose."[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-259)

*   [![Image 52: Bust at the University of Havana](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Alejandrodehumboldt.jpg/120px-Alejandrodehumboldt.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alejandrodehumboldt.jpg "Bust at the University of Havana")

*   [![Image 53: Statue in Budapester Straße, Berlin](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Alexander_von_Humboldt-Denkmal_in_der_Budapester_Str.%2C_Berlin_-_1.jpg/120px-Alexander_von_Humboldt-Denkmal_in_der_Budapester_Str.%2C_Berlin_-_1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alexander_von_Humboldt-Denkmal_in_der_Budapester_Str.,_Berlin_-_1.jpg "Statue in Budapester Straße, Berlin")

*   [![Image 54: Statue in Humboldt Park, Chicago](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Von_Humboldt_Statue.jpg/120px-Von_Humboldt_Statue.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Von_Humboldt_Statue.jpg "Statue in Humboldt Park, Chicago")

*   [![Image 55: Statue in Allegheny West Park, Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Statue_in_Allegheny_West_Park.jpg/120px-Alexander_von_Humboldt_Statue_in_Allegheny_West_Park.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alexander_von_Humboldt_Statue_in_Allegheny_West_Park.jpg "Statue in Allegheny West Park, Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania")

*   [![Image 60: Alexander Von Humboldt Statue. El Guácharo National Park. Monagas State. Venezuela](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Estatua_de_Alexander_Von_Humboldt._Parque_Nacional_El_Gu%C3%A1charo._Estado_Monagas._Venezuela..JPG/120px-Estatua_de_Alexander_Von_Humboldt._Parque_Nacional_El_Gu%C3%A1charo._Estado_Monagas._Venezuela..JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Estatua_de_Alexander_Von_Humboldt._Parque_Nacional_El_Gu%C3%A1charo._Estado_Monagas._Venezuela..JPG "Alexander Von Humboldt Statue. El Guácharo National Park. Monagas State. Venezuela")

Alexander Von Humboldt Statue. El Guácharo National Park. [Monagas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monagas "Monagas") State. Venezuela

*   [![Image 61: Humboldt, part of a sculpture in Cologne, Germany](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Standbild_Heumarkt_K%C3%B6ln_-_Alexander_von_Humboldt.jpg/120px-Standbild_Heumarkt_K%C3%B6ln_-_Alexander_von_Humboldt.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Standbild_Heumarkt_K%C3%B6ln_-_Alexander_von_Humboldt.jpg "Humboldt, part of a sculpture in Cologne, Germany")

Humboldt, part of [a sculpture](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Reiterstandbild_Friedrich_Wilhelm_III_in_K%C3%B6ln "commons:Category:Reiterstandbild Friedrich Wilhelm III in Köln") in Cologne, Germany

*   [![Image 62: Statue in Tower Grove Park, St. Louis[259]](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Humboldt-statue-tower-grove-benecke.jpg/120px-Humboldt-statue-tower-grove-benecke.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Humboldt-statue-tower-grove-benecke.jpg "Statue in Tower Grove Park, St. Louis[259]")

*   [![Image 63: Louis Agassiz and Alexander von Humboldt statues at Jordan Hall, Stanford University main quad](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Louis_Agassiz_and_Alexander_von_Humboldt_statues_at_Jordan_Hall%2C_Stanford.jpg/120px-Louis_Agassiz_and_Alexander_von_Humboldt_statues_at_Jordan_Hall%2C_Stanford.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Louis_Agassiz_and_Alexander_von_Humboldt_statues_at_Jordan_Hall,_Stanford.jpg "Louis Agassiz and Alexander von Humboldt statues at Jordan Hall, Stanford University main quad")

Louis Agassiz and Alexander von Humboldt statues at Jordan Hall, [Stanford University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University "Stanford University") main quad

*   [![Image 64: The bronze sculpture by the artist Ana Lilia Martín, born in La Palma (Canarias) in 1963, depicts the natural scientist Alexander von Humboldt. The sculpture has been on the terrace of the Humboldblick viewpoint in La Orotava since 2009.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Mirador_Humboldt_01.jpg/120px-Mirador_Humboldt_01.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mirador_Humboldt_01.jpg "The bronze sculpture by the artist Ana Lilia Martín, born in La Palma (Canarias) in 1963, depicts the natural scientist Alexander von Humboldt. The sculpture has been on the terrace of the Humboldblick viewpoint in La Orotava since 2009.")

The bronze sculpture by the artist Ana Lilia Martín, born in [La Palma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Palma "La Palma") (Canarias) in 1963, depicts the natural scientist Alexander von Humboldt. The sculpture has been on the terrace of the Humboldblick viewpoint in [La Orotava](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Orotava "La Orotava") since 2009.

*   [![Image 65: Sculpture in Chimborazo, Ecuador](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/B_Chimborazo_W_0501_054_%2816669362064%29.jpg/120px-B_Chimborazo_W_0501_054_%2816669362064%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:B_Chimborazo_W_0501_054_(16669362064).jpg "Sculpture in Chimborazo, Ecuador")

Sculpture in [Chimborazo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimborazo "Chimborazo"), Ecuador 

*   _Florae Fribergensis specimen plantas cryptogramicus praesertim subterraneas exhibens_, 1793. Humboldt's observations of underground plants made when he was a mining inspector.
*   _Versuche über die gereizte Muskel- und Nervenfaser nebst Versuchen über den chemischen Prozess des Lebens in der Thier- und Pflanzenwelt_. (2 volumes), 1797. Humboldt's experiments in galvanism and nerve conductivity.
*   [_Ueber die unterirdischen Gasarten und die Mittel, ihren Nachtheil zu vermindern_](https://books.google.com/books?id=NAJdttSLSxMC). Braunschweig: Vieweg 1799.
*   _Sur l'analyse de l'air atmosphérique_, with J.L. Gay-Lussac. Paris 1805. German edition, Türbingen.
*   _Fragments de géologie et de climatologie asiatiques_ 2 vols. Paris, 1831; Tübingen, 1831
*   _Asie centrale, recherches sur les chaînes des montagnes et la climotologie comparée_. 3 vols. 1843

_Le voyage aux régions equinoxiales du Nouveau Continent, fait en 1799–1804, par Alexandre de Humboldt et Aimé Bonpland_ (Paris, 1807, etc.), consisted of thirty folio and quarto volumes, including:

*   _Vues des Cordillères et monuments des peuples indigènes de l'Amérique_ (2 vols. folio, 1810) 
    *   English translation: [_Researches concerning the institutions & monuments of the ancient inhabitants of America: with descriptions & views of some of the most striking scenes in the Cordilleras!_ (2 vols.)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/125538) [exclamation point in the original title]
    *   English translation: _Views of the Cordilleras and Monuments of the Indigenous Peoples of the Americas: A Critical Edition_. [Vera M. Kutzinski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vera_Kutzinski "Vera Kutzinski") and [Ottmar Ette](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottmar_Ette "Ottmar Ette"), editors. Chicago: University of Chicago Press, 2014. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)")[978-0-226-86506-5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-226-86506-5 "Special:BookSources/978-0-226-86506-5")

*   _[Examen critique de l'histoire de la géographie du Nouveau Continent](https://archive.org/details/examencritiqued06humbgoog)_ (4 vols. 1814–1834)
*   _Atlas géographique et physique du royaume de la Nouvelle Espagne_ (1811)
*   [_Essai politique sur le royaume de la Nouvelle Espagne_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/85270#page/8/mode/1up) (1811); 
    *   English translation: [_Political essay on the kingdom of New Spain containing researches relative to the geography of Mexico_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/85282#page/12/mode/1up), (1811) biodiversitylibrary.org;

*   [_Essai sur la géographie des plantes: accompagné d'un tableau physique des régions équinoxiales, fondé sur des mesures exécutées, depuis le dixième degré de latitude boréale jusqu'au dixième degré de latitude australe, pendant les années 1799, 1800, 1801, 1802 et 1803/ par Al. de Humboldt et A. Bonpland; rédigée par Al. de Humboldt_ (1805)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/37872), biodiversitylibrary.org 
    *   English translation by Sylvie Romanowski:_Essay on the Geography of Plants_. University of Chicago Press. (2009)

*   _Essai géognostique sur le gisement des roches dans les deux continents_. Paris 1823. English and German editions.
*   _Essai politique sur l'îsle de Cuba_. 2 vols. Paris 1828. English[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-261) and German editions.
*   [_Relation historique du Voyage aux Régions équinoxiales du Nouveau Continent, etc._ (1814–1825), an unfinished narrative of his travels, including the _Essai politique sur l'île de Cuba_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/95419), biodiversitylibrary.org
*   [_Monographie des melastomacées_ (1833)](http://cdm15121.contentdm.oclc.org/cdm4/document.php?CISOROOT=/p9016coll23&CISOPTR=1299&REC=4)
*   [_Monographia Melastomacearum: continens plantas huius ordinis, hucusque collectas, praesertim per regnum Mexici, in provinciis Caracarum et Novae Andalusiae, in Peruvianorum, Quitensium, Novae Granatae Andibus, ad Orinoci, fluvii Nigri, fluminis Amazonum rupas nascentes_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/16027) (2 vols.)
*   [_Cosmos: a sketch of a physical description of the universe by Alexander von Humboldt; translated from the German by E. C. Otté_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/32462) (5 vols.)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-262)
*   [_Cosmos: essai d'une description physique du monde_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/40012) (4 vols.)
*   [_Gesammelte Werke von Alexander von Humboldt_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/33954) (12 vols.)
*   [_Ansichten der Natur: mit wissenschaftlichen Erläuterungen_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/23794)
*   [_Aphorismen aus der chemischen Physiologie der Pflanzen. Aus dem Lateinischen übersetzt von Gotthelf Fischer. Nebst einigen Zusätzen von Herrn Dr. und Prof. Hedwig und einer Vorrede von Herrn Dr. und Prof. Christ. Friedr. Ludwig_.](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/101629) 1794.
*   [_Aspects of nature, in different lands and different climates with scientific elucidations_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/45601)
*   [_Atlas zu Alex. v. Humboldt's Kosmos in zweiundvierzig Tafeln mit erläuterndem Texte / herausgegeben von Traugott Bromme_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/89025#page/1/mode/1up)
*   [_Briefe von Alexander von Humboldt an Varnhagen von Ense, aus den Jahren 1827 bis 1858: nebst Auszügen aus Varnhagen's Tagebüchern und Briefen von Varnhagen und andern an Humboldt_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/60882#page/7/mode/1up)
*   [_Ideen zu einer Geographie der Pflanzen: nebst einem Naturgemälde der Tropenländer: auf Beobachtungen und Messungen gegründet, welche vom 10ten Grade nördlicher bis zum 10ten Grade südlicher Breite, in den Jahren 1799, 1800, 1801, 1802 und 1803 angestellt worden sind / von Al. von Humboldt und A. Bonpland; bearbeitet und herausgegeben von dem erstern_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/37871#page/1/mode/1up)
*   [_An illustration of the genus Cinchona :comprising descriptions of all the officinal Peruvian barks, including several new species, Baron de Humboldt's Account of the Cinchona forests of South America, and Laubert's Memoir on the different species of quinquina: to which are added several dissertations of Don Hippolito Ruiz on various medicinal plants of South America_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/14437) (1821);
*   [_Kosmos. Entwurf einer physischen Weltbeschreibung von Alexander von Humboldt_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/4717) (5 vols.)
*   _Des lignes isothermes et de la distribution de la châleur sur le globe_. Paris 1817. German edition, Türbingen.
*   [_Personal narrative of travels to the equinoctial regions of America, during the years 1799–1804/ by Alexander von Humboldt and Aimé Bonpland; translated from the French of Alexander von Humboldt and edited by Thomasina Ross_ (vols 2 & 3)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/23548), biodiversitylibrary.org
*   _Personal Narrative of Travels to the Equinoctial Regions of the New Continent_. 7 vols. London. First edition in French, Paris: 1815–26.
*   [_Viage âa las regiones equinocciales del nuevo continente: hecho en 1799 hasta 1804, por Al. de Humboldt y A. Bonpland; redactado por Alejandro de Humboldt; continuaciâon indispensable al ensayo polâitico sobre el reino de la Nueva Espaäna por el mismo autor_ (5 vols.)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/25297), 1826. biodiversitylibrary.org
*   [_Pflanzengeographie, nach Alexander von Humboldt's Werke ueber die geographische Vertheilhung der Gewächse: mit Anmerkungen, grösseren Beilagen aus andern pflanzengeographischen Schriften und einem Excurse über die bei pflanzengeographischen Floren-Vergleichungen nöthigen Rücksichten_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/109430)
*   [_Plantes équinoxiales recueillies au Mexique :dans l'île de Cuba, dans les provinces de Caracas, de Cumana et de Barcelone, aux Andes de la Nouvelle Grenade, de Quito et du Pérou, et sur les bords du rio-Negro de Orénoque et de la rivière des Amazones_ (2 vols.)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/460)
*   [_Recueil d'observations de zoologie et d'anatomie comparée: faites dans l'océan atlantique, dans l'intérieur du nouveau continent et dans la mer du sud pendant les années 1799, 1800, 1801, 1802 et 1803 / par Al. de Humboldt et A. Bonpland_ (2 vols.)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/43770)
*   [_Reise in die Aequinoctial-Gegenden des neuen Continents in den Jahren 1799, 1800, 1801, 1803 und 1804_ (vol. 3)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/73180)
*   [_Relation historique du voyage aux régions équinoxiales du nouveau continent, fait en 1799, 1800, 1801, 1802, 1803, et 1804_ (vol. 3)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/95419)
*   [_Tableaux de la nature; ou, Considérations sur les déserts, sur le physionomie des végétaux, sur les cataractes de l'Orénoque, sur la structure et l'action des volcans dans les différentes régions de la terre_](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/89305)
*   [_Views of nature, or, Contemplations on the sublime phenomena of creation: with scientific illustrations_ (1850)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/24009)
*   [_Views of nature: or, Contemplations on the sublime phenomena of creation; with scientific illustrations_ (1884)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/72102)

*   [_Letters of Alexander von Humboldt to Varnhagen von Ense. From 1827 to 1858. With extracts from Varnhagen's diaries, and letters of Varnhagen and others to Humboldt_. Tr. from the 2d German by Friedrich Kapp (ed.)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/79321), biodiversitylibrary.org
*   [_Letters of Alexander von Humboldt written between the years 1827 and 1858 to Varnhagen von Ense together with extracts from Varnhagen's diaries, and letters of Varnhagen and others to Humboldt/ authorized translation from the German_ (with explanatory notes and a full index of names)](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/78470), biodiversitylibrary.org
*   [_Nova genera et species plantarum_ (7 vols. folio, 1815–1825), contains descriptions of above 4500 species of plants collected by Humboldt and Bonpland](https://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/640), was mainly compiled by [Carl Sigismund Kunth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Sigismund_Kunth "Carl Sigismund Kunth"); J. Oltmanns assisted in preparing the _Recueil d'observations astronomiques_ (1808); Cuvier, Latreille, Valenciennes and Gay-Lussac cooperated in the _Recueil d'observations de zoologie et d'anatomie comparée_ (1805–1833).[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt#cite_note-EB1911-23)
